Bozcaada ==&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Hi Aervanath, I see that you have closed the discussion on the move request of Tenedos. Being the admin you have the power to do that. But being an editor in the discuss?on I have the right to ask the reason, especially after seing the majority-support. The island is named Bozcaada for the last 500 years or so. It is an unimportant island notable only because it is a district of Turkey. Tenedos on the other hand is a mythological name and it has nothing to do with the present island district. Well, the opposers put forward the principle of more-English sources. But they are wrong, most of the Tenedos sources are about the mythology and not about the present Bozcaada.  Moreover in WP as I have shown in the discussion, more-English source principle is no more applied rigorously.  (Mumbai and Beijing for example) I suggest you review your decision about closing the discussion. Cheers. Many thanks, [[User:Girolamo Savonarola|Girolamo Savonarola]] ([[User talk:Girolamo Savonarola|talk]]) 03:28, 13 October 2008 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Help request: 34 Côte d'Ivoire-related articles needing geographical coordinates==&lt;br /&gt;, Based on a search of Wikipedia's articles related to Côte d'Ivoire, I've found some articles that I believe are about places in Côte d'Ivoire, and could usefully have [[geographical coordinates]] added.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The articles in question are listed in [[:Category:Côte d'Ivoire articles missing geocoordinate data]].  At the time of writing, some examples included:&lt;br /&gt;, # [[Bocanda]]&lt;br /&gt;, # [[Bongouanou]]&lt;br /&gt;, # [[Boule (Community)]]&lt;br /&gt;, # [[Béoumi]]&lt;br /&gt;, # [[Mankono]]&lt;br /&gt;, # [[Mont Sângbé National Park]]&lt;br /&gt;, # [[Prikro]]&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ...and there are many more, as well. At the time of posting this notice, there were 34 articles in this category needing geographical coordinates.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===Why add coordinates?===&lt;br /&gt;, By adding coordinates, a Wikipedia reader can easily view the location on a street map, nautical chart, topographic map, by satellite photo, realtime weather map, and in many other ways. Coordinate data makes an article eventually appear in various services such as [[Google Maps]]' Wikipedia overlay, [[Google Earth]], and Wikipedia's own internal map service.  Coordinate data also helps readers looking for geographically-based data, such as locations near a reference point, or related information.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===How can I do it?===&lt;br /&gt;, The articles are all marked with {{tl|coord missing}} tags, which need to be replaced with {{tl|coord}} tags that contain the location's latitude/longitude coordinates; or you might be able to add coordinates to an existing [[WP:Infobox|infobox]]. You can find out how to do this at the [[Wikipedia:Geocoding how-to for WikiProject members]]. Please let me know if this is useful, or if you have any questions! -- [[User:The Anome|The Anome]] ([[User talk:The Anome|talk]]) 11:39, 24 October 2008 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Images available for upload ==&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, [http://www.flickr.com/photos/stefanmeisel/2555194197/ This user at Flickr] has a number of photos which are CC-BY licensed (and thus available to upload to http://commons.wikimedia.org. He has a pile of picture (''some''freely licensed, some not) of the CI national squad training in Abidjan, dignitaries and celebrities, and the city. I've got other stuff to do, but any image by this user with the little &lt;br /&gt;, &amp;quot;(BY)  Attribution  Some rights reserved &amp;quot; tag can be uploaded and used on Wikipedia freely. Have at it. Additional information is available at the [[Wikipedia talk:Version 1.0 Editorial Team/Index|WP 1.0 project homepage]]. &amp;amp;mdash;&amp;amp;nbsp;Carl &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;([[User:CBM|CBM]]&amp;amp;nbsp;·&amp;amp;nbsp;[[User talk:CBM|talk]])&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt; 03:11, 22 January 2010 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Unreferenced living people articles bot== &lt;br /&gt;, {{User:DASHBot/Wikiprojects/welcome}} [[User:Okip |Okip ]]  01:09, 28 March 2010 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == [[Talk:Côte d'Ivoire|RFC: Côte d'Ivoire or Ivory Coast]] ==&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, To note that there is a request for comment on whether Wikipedia should be giving primacy to the phrase of Côte d'Ivoire or Ivory Coast. Those who would like to express their opinion and participate in the discussion should do at that talk page. [[user:billinghurst|billinghurst]] ''&amp;lt;span style=&amp;quot;font-size:smaller&amp;quot;&amp;gt;[[user talk:billinghurst|sDrewth]]&amp;lt;/span&amp;gt;'' 08:30, 12 July 2010 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Cote d'Ivoire articles have been selected for the Wikipedia 0.8 release ==&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Version 0.8 is a collection of Wikipedia articles selected by the [[Wikipedia:Version_1.0_Editorial_Team|Wikipedia 1.0 team]] for offline release on USB key, DVD and mobile phone.  Articles were [[Wikipedia:Version 1.0 Editorial Team/Article selection|selected based on their assessed  importance and quality]], then article ''versions'' (revisionIDs) were chosen for trustworthiness (freedom from vandalism) using an adaptation of the [[WikiTrust]] algorithm.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, We would like to ask you to review the [http://toolserver.org/~enwp10/bin/list2.fcgi?run=yes&amp;amp;namespace=0&amp;amp;pagename=&amp;amp;quality=&amp;amp;importance=&amp;amp;score=&amp;amp;limit=100&amp;amp;offset=1&amp;amp;sorta=Importance&amp;amp;sortb=Quality&amp;amp;filterRelease=on&amp;amp;reviewFilter=0&amp;amp;releaseFilter=1&amp;amp;projecta=Cote%20d'Ivoire Cote d'Ivoire articles and revisionIDs we have chosen]. Selected articles are marked with a diamond symbol (&amp;amp;diams;) to the right of each article, and this symbol links to the selected version of each article. If you believe we have included or excluded articles inappropriately, please contact us at '''[[Wikipedia talk:Version 0.8]]''' with the details.  You may wish to look at your WikiProject's [http://toolserver.org/~cbm/cgi-bin/problems.cgi articles with cleanup tags] and try to improve any that need work; if you do, please give us the new revisionID at [[Wikipedia talk:Version 0.8]]. We would like to complete this consultation period by midnight UTC on Sunday, November 14th. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, We have greatly streamlined the process since the Version 0.7 release, so we aim to have the collection ready for distribution by the end  of November, 2010.  As a result, we are planning to distribute the collection much more widely, while continuing to work with groups such as [[One Laptop per Child]] and [http://schools-wikipedia.org/ Wikipedia for Schools] to extend the reach of Wikipedia worldwide.  Please help us, with [[Wikipedia_talk:Version_0.8|your WikiProject's feedback]]! &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, If you have already provided feedback, we deeply appreciate it. To edit my request the key is: j8778ge. --[[User:Kleopatra|Kleopatra]] ([[User talk:Kleopatra|talk]]) 17:12, 9 November 2010 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Pageview stats ==&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, After a recent request, I added WikiProject Côte d'Ivoire to the list of projects to compile monthly pageview stats for. The data is the same used by http://stats.grok.se/en/ but the program is different, and includes the aggregate views from all redirects to each page. The stats are at [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Côte d'Ivoire/Popular pages]].&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The page will be updated monthly with new data. The edits aren't marked as bot edits, so they will show up in watchlists. You can view more results, request a new project be added to the list, or request a configuration change for this project using the [[tools:~alexz/pop/|toolserver tool]]. If you have any comments or suggestions, please let me know. [[User:Marcus Qwertyus|Marcus Qwertyus]] ([[User talk:Marcus Qwertyus|talk]]) 05:38, 3 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :::::::I asked for an opinion from [[WP:COUNCIL]], where an opinion given said it's probably a bad thing, since it could make editors stop editing. -- [[Special:Contributions/76.65.131.248|76.65.131.248]] ([[User talk:76.65.131.248|talk]]) 22:56, 14 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::::::::Just to be clear, this is the [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Council#WikiProject naming|opinion of an individual]]. Your comment made me think that the council as a body handed down an opinion. That said, the opinion probably suggests a legitimate concern. --[[User:BDD|BDD]] ([[User talk:BDD|talk]]) 15:55, 15 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Mild Oppose''' - I tend to think that, despite the recent moves elsewhere, that &amp;quot;Cote d'Ivoire&amp;quot; is one of only two countries, the other being &amp;quot;Timor Leste&amp;quot; who have come to prominence since the people in the US and UK have become a bit less, well, English-centric, and that, despite the recent discussion of moving, this actually is, at present, the more commonly used form of the name in the academic world. It may even be becoming such in the regular news media as well. The fact of one page being named does not, as per policy, mean that any and all other pages must similarly be changed. Personally, I think it would be an extraordinary effort to change the templates to reflect this proposed change, change the relevant categories for assessment, ans so on and on and on, particularly when this matter is less clearcut than some might think. I honestly can't see any particular benefit from the name change, and a possibly extreme amount of work to be imposed on someone simply because they want to go possibly a bit overboard and seemingly remove a name which is in use, even if not in the most regular way, in the English speaking press. However, if someone else wishes to engage in the effort to change the assessment categories, banner material, and so on, then I would have no objection. But, honestly, it makes no sense to me to have the categories be for the Cote d'Ivoire topic when the project itself is perhaps Ivory Coast. /&gt;,  | csb = yes&lt;br /&gt;, | assessment = [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Africa/Assessment|/Assessment]]&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, Bonjour! and Welcome to the '''WikiProject Côte d'Ivoire'''! This group was formed to better organize articles on [[Côte d'Ivoire]] in a spirit of cooperation.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Scope==&lt;br /&gt;, This group includes within its scope all articles related to Côte d'Ivoire, its cities, geography, transportation, culture, history and so on. It aims to expand Wikipedia's resources on Côte d'Ivoire in a fair and accurate manner. All of these articles should be contained within the [[:Category:Côte d'Ivoire]] or one of its subcategories.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==What you can do==&lt;br /&gt;, * Work on articles relating to Côte d'Ivoire [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Africa#Needing work|Tagged as needing work in the AfricaProject]] .   &lt;br /&gt;, * Assess the [[:Category:Unassessed Cote dIvoire articles|Unassessed Cote d'Ivoire articles]] as Stub, Start, B-Class, etc. More on assessment [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Africa/Assessment|here]].&lt;br /&gt;, * Tag all Côte d'Ivoire-relevant articles with &amp;lt;nowiki&amp;gt;{{AfricaProject | class= |CI=yes}}&amp;lt;/nowiki&amp;gt; and an assessment.&lt;br /&gt;, * Add your name to the WikiProject Côte d'Ivoire  members list (below), and to the members list of our parent [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Africa]].&lt;br /&gt;, * Invite more users to join [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Africa/Inviting members|WikiProject Africa]] with knowledge of or interest in Cote d'Ivoire.&lt;br /&gt;, * Create all yet-uncreated project pages (those in red). Sort through [[Wikipedia:List of_missing_Africa topics|Wikipedia:List of missing Africa topics]] for Côte d'Ivoire related requests.&lt;br /&gt;, * Create Cote d'Ivoire subcategories and populate the created categories.  Remove items from [[:Category:Côte d'Ivoire]] that ought to be in subcategories.&lt;br /&gt;, * Create basic Côte d'Ivoire topic articles: see [[User:TUF-KAT/Topics by country]] for a list of links for every nation/every basic topic.&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Portal:Africa/Things you can do|More things to do...]]&lt;br /&gt;, * Add more things about national and sports teams of the Côte D'Ivoire&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===Upcoming events===&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===Template===&lt;br /&gt;, Please add tag Côte d'Ivoire-related article by modifying or adding the WikiProject Africa tag, like so:&lt;br /&gt;, &amp;lt;div style=&amp;quot;width: 530px; align: left; background: #dddddd; border: 1px solid black; padding:0.5em 1em 0.5em 1em;&amp;quot;&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &amp;lt;pre&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, {{AfricaProject&lt;br /&gt;, |Class=List/Stub/Start/B/&lt;br /&gt;, |importance=Low/Mid/High/Top&lt;br /&gt;, |CI=yes&lt;br /&gt;, |CI-importance= Low/Mid/High/Top&lt;br /&gt;, }}&amp;lt;/pre&amp;gt;&amp;lt;/div&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, Note that these tags are case sensitive.&lt;br /&gt;, Please see {{tl|AfricaProject}} for more information on the template, as well as assessment information.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===Article alerts===&lt;br /&gt;, {{/Article alerts}}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Participants==&lt;br /&gt;, If you haven't already done so, please also add your name to the members list of our parent [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Africa]].&lt;br /&gt;, *[[User:John Carter|John Carter]] 18:09, 3 December 2007 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *--[[User:Zenman|Zenman]] ([[User talk:Zenman|talk]]) 07:51, 13 September 2008 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *[[User:CôteD'Ivoire2|CôteD'Ivoire2]] 16:08, 1 August 2009 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *[[User:Bcorr|BCorr]]&amp;lt;font color=&amp;quot;chartreuse&amp;quot;&amp;gt;|&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt;[[User talk:Bcorr|??????]] 18:32, 12 August 2009 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *--[[User:Kleopatra|Kleopatra]] ([[User talk:Kleopatra|talk]]) 17:10, 9 November 2010 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, Members should also feel free to add {{tl|User WikiProject Côte d'Ivoire}} to their userpages to identify themselves as members of this group.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Requests==&lt;br /&gt;, ===Image requests===&lt;br /&gt;, In addition to posting your image requests on the list, on the talk page(s) of the subject(s), and on the Wikimedia Commons ([[:Commons:Commons:Picture requests]]), please also post them at [[:fr:Wikipédia:Atelier photographique]] on the French Wikipedia. The album I've owned for many years, (purchased in 1976) includes &amp;quot;Please Take Your Drunken Fifteen Year Old Girlfriend Home&amp;quot;, and omits the tracks &amp;quot;Cliches&amp;quot;, and &amp;quot;Defying Gravity&amp;quot;. There are two slightly different versions of &amp;quot;Kick It In Second Wind&amp;quot;.&lt;br /&gt;, &amp;quot;15 Year Old Girlfriend&amp;quot; is one of my favorite Buffett songs. The lyrics are amusing, and it has a catchy groove to it.&lt;br /&gt;, When I lived in San Diego in the late eighties and early nineties, a DJ on KLOS in L.A. used to kick off the weekend with a trio of songs and &amp;quot;15 Year old Girlfriend&amp;quot; was one of them.&lt;br /&gt;, [[User:KC49er|KC49er]] ([[User talk:KC49er|talk]]) 01:33, 28 September 2008 (UTC)KC49ers&lt;br /&gt;, ==Fair use rationale for Image:JimmyBuffettHavanaDaydreamin'.jpg==&lt;br /&gt;, [[Image:Nuvola apps important.svg|70px|left]]&lt;br /&gt;, '''[[:Image:JimmyBuffettHavanaDaydreamin'.jpg]]''' is being used on this article. I notice the image page specifies that the image is being used under [[Wikipedia:Fair use|fair use]] but there is no [[Wikipedia:Fair use rationale guideline|explanation or rationale]] as to why its use in '''this''' Wikipedia article constitutes fair use. In addition to the [[Wikipedia:Image copyright tags/Fair use|boilerplate fair use template]], you must also write out on the image description page a specific explanation or rationale for why using this image in each article is consistent with [[WP:FU|fair use]].&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Please go to [[:Image:JimmyBuffettHavanaDaydreamin'.jpg|the image description page]] and edit it to include a [[Wikipedia:Fair use rationale guideline |fair use rationale]]. Using one of the templates at [[Wikipedia:Fair use rationale guideline]] is an easy way to insure that your image is in compliance with Wikipedia policy, but remember that you must complete the template. Do not simply insert a blank template on an image page.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, If there is other other fair use media, consider checking that you have specified the fair use rationale on the other images used on this page.  Note that any fair use images uploaded after 4 May, 2006, and lacking such an explanation will be deleted one week after they have been uploaded, as described on [[Wikipedia:Criteria for speedy deletion#Images.2FMedia|criteria for speedy deletion]]. If you have any questions please ask them at the [[Wikipedia:Media copyright questions|Media copyright questions page]]. Thank you.&amp;lt;!-- Template:Missing rationale2 --&amp;gt;[[User:BetacommandBot|BetacommandBot]] 07:06, 5 June 2007 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Requested move ==&lt;br /&gt;, &amp;lt;div class=&amp;quot;boilerplate&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;background-color: #efe; margin: 2em 0 0 0; padding: 0 10px 0 10px; border: 1px dotted #aaa;&amp;quot;&amp;gt;&amp;lt;!-- Template:RM top --&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, :''The following discussion is an archived discussion of a [[WP:requested moves|requested move]]. &amp;lt;span style=&amp;quot;color:red&amp;quot;&amp;gt;'''Please do not modify it.'''&amp;lt;/span&amp;gt; Subsequent comments should be made in a new section on the talk page. Editors desiring to contest the closing decision should consider a [[Wikipedia:move review|move review]]. No further edits should be made to this section. ''&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The result of the move request was: '''moved.''' Wikipedia always follows [[WP:RS|reliable sources]], and &amp;quot;Wikipedia articles should be based mainly on reliable ''secondary'' sources.&amp;quot; If the secondary sources we have refer to the title without the tilde, then we use the title without the tilde, whatever the &amp;quot;original&amp;quot; name of the album/track was intended to be. [[User:Aervanath|Aervanath]] ([[User talk:Aervanath|talk]]) 19:50, 4 October 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ----&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, [[Havaña Daydreamin&amp;amp;#39;]] ? {{no redirect|Havana Daydreamin'}}  The proper name of the album (and its title track of the same name) is &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot;, no tilde.  Never was one.  (See here for reputable source documenting this: http://www.artistdirect.com/nad/store/artist/album/0,,58877,00.html.)  A page by the proper name pre-existed, someone erroneously corrected it to the Spanish language form for the word &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot; (with a tilde).  The errant redirect needs to be undone, and all references to &amp;quot;Havaña&amp;quot; in the (restored) page corrected to &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot;.  Please advise me when the move is complete and I will undertake these latter edits.  Thank you.  [[User:Wikiuser100|Wikiuser100]] ([[User talk:Wikiuser100|talk]]) 00:14, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :'''Not sure'''. Our copy of the album cover image is very low-res and does not clearly show the title lettering, but a full-size image of the album cover clearly shows &amp;quot;Havaña&amp;quot; (searching &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot; at http://images.google.com/ gives many examples, for instance http://whenyouputitthatway.wordpress.com/2012/03/11/appreciating-jimmy-buffett/ ). On the other hand, listening to the title song (on YouTube or elsewhere), it is clearly pronounced &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot;, presumably about the city, and not with the &amp;quot;'ny'-as-in-'canyon'&amp;quot; sound of n-tilde. So this is clearly the tilde equivalent of a [[heavy-metal umlaut]].  The question is, how do we handle this?  We could do something similar to the [[Spinal Tap]] article, keeping it at the non-diacritic title but mentioning the diacritical &amp;quot;flourish&amp;quot; in the lede (I will attempt an edit).  But do we have Spinal Tap at the non-diacritic title because that's the best choice, or simply as a practical matter because n-umlaut is more or less nonexistent in real usage and the diacritic title would not display properly for many users.  [[User:P.T. Aufrette|P.T. Aufrette]] ([[User talk:P.T. Aufrette|talk]]) 02:52, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, * '''&amp;lt;s&amp;gt;Also not sure&amp;lt;/s&amp;gt;''' I must say it irks a bit to see Havana mispelled like that, but it clearly is there on the 1976 LP cover and hasn't been photo-shopped out in the CD reissue. Given the lyrics ''&amp;quot;Stashed his trash in Ecuador / Bought a good suit of clothes / Flew on up to Mexico / Standin' by the shore / Waitin' for some mystery&amp;quot;'' and the apparent reputation of general irony of Jimmy Buffet's Caribbean books and records, have to assume that this is a deliberate stylistic &amp;quot;heavy metal umlaut&amp;quot; as P.T. Aufrette says, not just a mistake. The fact that Havana is overlatinised with a mistaken tilde may be connected with the lyrics' irony about a gringo in Latinland? Who knows. But whatever we can't simply correct it because Havana doesn't have a tilde in real life. I would think first priority is to actually mention the oddity in the lede, not simply remove it as a recent edit has done. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 03:22, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, **'''Oppose''' Stero Review (1976) noted the &amp;quot;mistake,&amp;quot; see source now in article. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 03:49, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Oppose'''.  It's a [[metal umlaut|gulf and western tilde]].  The original release ([http://www.discogs.com/viewimages?release=1297706 images]), the 1980 MCA release ([http://www.discogs.com/viewimages?release=3451888 images]), and the CD release of the album (on the cover and the CD itself, but not on the spine label) all use the tilde.  ''Cf''. [[Mötley Crüe (album)|''Mötley Crüe'' (album)]], ''[[March ör Die]]'', ''[[Ænima]]'', and of course [[Rinôçérôse (album)|''Rinôçérôse'' (album)]].   [[User talk:AjaxSmack|&amp;lt;span style=&amp;quot;border:1px solid #000073;background:#4D4DA6;padding:2px;color:#F9FFFF;text-shadow:black 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em&amp;quot;&amp;gt;&amp;lt;font face=&amp;quot;Georgia&amp;quot;&amp;gt;&amp;amp;nbsp;'''AjaxSmack'''&amp;amp;nbsp;&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt;&amp;lt;/span&amp;gt;]] 03:37, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Support''', per [http://www.worldcat.org/title/havana-daydreamin/oclc/178729216&amp;amp;referer=brief_results WorldCat], [http://www.amazon.com/Havana-Daydreamin/dp/B000W11MM2/ref=sr_1_4?ie=UTF8&amp;amp;qid=1345520957&amp;amp;sr=8-4&amp;amp;keywords=Havana+Daydreamin%27 Amazon], [http://www.cduniverse.com/search/xx/music/pid/1104335/a/Havana+Daydreamin'.htm CD Universe], [http://www.allmusic.com/album/havana-daydreamin-mw0000194138 AllMusic], and the ''[http://books.google.com.vn/books?id=D5Wq1LM7-84C&amp;amp;q=Havana+Daydreamin#search_anchor Standard Catalog of American Records]''. Everyone called it ''Havana Daydreamin`'' even when the official name had a diacritic. It looks like the diacritic-free form is the title proper for the CD, i.e. it has been the official name since 1987. [[User:Kauffner|Kauffner]] ([[User talk:Kauffner|talk]]) 04:42, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::The Amazon CD image clearly shows the &amp;quot;ambiguous journey into B. Traven&amp;quot; tilde. Whether Amazon's inputters can/do input Spanish (particularly incorrect pseudo-Spanish) into indexing is not germane here. [Can't see the track-listing of course, to see whether it is still as the LP or has been dehumorised....] [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 07:09, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :::Album covers are like book covers. They are just art. If the diacritic was part of the title proper, WorldCat would give it. [[User:Kauffner|Kauffner]] ([[User talk:Kauffner|talk]]) 07:32, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::::Are you a librarian, Kauffner? This is a pretty good description of how we catalog, by [[Anglo-American Cataloguing Rules|AACR2]]. If it was cataloged as &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin',&amp;quot; that's what was on the album itself, assuming the cataloger didn't make any mistakes. When cataloging records or CDs, the title on the disc is the &amp;quot;title proper&amp;quot; for librarians. I'm not sure how much it informs this debate, however. --[[User:BDD|BDD]] ([[User talk:BDD|talk]]) 18:21, 4 October 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Oppose'''. I dug out my original '70s LP and sure enough the tilde is on the cover and vinyl album's Side A song list.  Had long since faded from memory (due initially to Buffett ignoring its pronunciation, then decades of it not being used even in the US music media (per current example of artistsdirect.com cited at the start of this thread)).  If we were rewriting history and adding one where it never had been I would continue to oppose its use; accepting reality is something else.  Should have rooted out the old LP to begin with. [[User:Wikiuser100|Wikiuser100]] ([[User talk:Wikiuser100|talk]]) 18:29, 24 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Support'''. This is the epitome of what [[MOS:TM]] is referring to when it says &amp;quot;Avoid using special characters that are not pronounced, are '''included purely for decoration''', or simply substitute for English words (e.g., ? used for &amp;quot;love&amp;quot;).&amp;quot; The title is recorded sans tilda in all the sources currently used, as well as, for instance, here: [http://www.amazon.com/Havana-Daydreamin-Jimmy-Buffett/dp/B000002PBZ][http://www.postandcourier.com/article/20080323/PC1602/303239998][http://jacksonville.com/entertainment/music/2012-01-27/story/discover-jimmy-buffetts-lost-musical-treasures]--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 19:04, 13 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::Hmm, I've had so much recent experience of following MOS pages and then finding they've been edit-warred by editors at odds with article-reality that I daren't even look. If it applies to music it may just mean that whoever's edit is on top there has a problem with articles like [[Mötley Crüe]]. But as above Stero Review (1976) noted the &amp;quot;mistake,&amp;quot; and that source is now in article. We don't know it is &amp;quot;included purely for decoration&amp;quot;, but what does &amp;quot;included purely for decoration&amp;quot; mean anyway? Isn't [[Häagen-Dazs]] purely decoration, designed to trick consumers into thinking it's a Swedish product? I'd still prefer to go with the physical album cover and Stereo Review picking up on it than MOS edits which appear to be at odds with [[Mötley Crüe]] en.wp reality. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 06:58, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :::As you know we follow what the secondary sources say above whatever appeared on the album in the 1970s. Unlike the example of Motley Crue, in this case they virtually all eschew the tilda, evidently including the Stereo Review source after the first mention where they note the error. The sources do this because this is an unpronounced, unaddressed decorative element, or else an error, neither of which warrant us including it against use in the sources.--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 13:13, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::::Yeah, well in any case [[User:Wikiuser100|Wikiuser100]] no longer supports his own proposal. Besides I'm not sure we have many secondary sources other than Stero Review (1976). Stan Zimmerman uses Ponce de León so he counts (against by omission) the mispelled Havana... but otherwise the sources don't carry Spanish even when correct. I'm not particularly bothered, as I (the [[Spanish orthography]] part of me) would like to correct it. Given he doesn't mention the song in his own books, maybe someone should email him? Anyway this has been an interesting/entertaining little time-waster. Cheers. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 10:20, 19 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :::::Once again, it doesn't matter what Buffett calls it, it matters what the sources call it. The only source we've seen that includes it is Stereo Review, which merely notes the error with a [''sic''] - and then calls it &amp;quot;Hava'''n'''a Daydreamin'&amp;quot; elsewhere in the text. Of the other sources, Allmusic.com is [http://www.allmusic.com/album/carlos-nunez-en-concert-mw0000742788 clearly capable] of using diacritics, but avoids them with this album.[http://www.allmusic.com/album/havana-daydreamin-mw0000194138] Whether the other sources use Spanish orthography in general is immaterial, since this isn't Spanish orthography, it's just a decorative (and erroneous) element on an English-language album. At any rate, they certainly don't use the tilda. We have specific guidelines against using these things; this case is pretty clear cut.--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 15:01, 19 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::::::[http://books.google.com/books?id=YVd0A6hluCUC&amp;amp;pg=PA131&amp;amp;lpg=PA131&amp;amp;dq=%22Havana+Daydreamin%27%22+%22b+traven%22&amp;amp;source=bl&amp;amp;ots=ZGsP1hPGKv&amp;amp;sig=e0cGeINIlnTTWXYCzapxnUVLjgY&amp;amp;hl=en&amp;amp;sa=X&amp;amp;ei=b6FpUNGEO5Co8QTqz4CAAQ&amp;amp;ved=0CCwQ6AEwAg#v=onepage&amp;amp;q=%22Havana%20Daydreamin%27%22&amp;amp;f=false This book] also calls it &amp;quot;Hava'''n'''a Daydreamin'&amp;quot;, and suggests our current cite of the ''Stereo Review'' piece is incomplete.--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 14:01, 1 October 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :''The above discussion is preserved as an archive of a [[WP:RM|requested move]].  &amp;lt;span style=&amp;quot;color:red&amp;quot;&amp;gt;'''Please do not modify it.'''&amp;lt;/span&amp;gt; Subsequent comments should be made in a new section on this talk page or in a [[WP:move review|move review]]. &lt;p&gt;Aervanath: Aervanath moved page Havaña Daydreamin' to Havana Daydreamin': see discussion on talk page&lt;/p&gt;, &lt;hr /&gt;, &lt;div&gt;{{Infobox album &amp;lt;!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Albums --&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, | Name        = Havana Daydreamin'&lt;br /&gt;, | Type        = [[Album]]&lt;br /&gt;, | Artist      = [[Jimmy Buffett]]&lt;br /&gt;, | Cover       = JimmyBuffettHavanaDaydreamin'.jpg&lt;br /&gt;, | Released    = January 1976&lt;br /&gt;, | Recorded    = 1975&lt;br /&gt;, | Genre       = [[Rock music|Rock]]/[[Gulf and western (music genre)|Gulf and western]]&lt;br /&gt;, | Length      = 33:08&lt;br /&gt;, | Label       = [[ABC Dunhill Records|ABC Dunhill]]&amp;lt;br /&amp;gt;&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;ABCD-914 ([[United States|U.S.]], [[gramophone record|12&amp;quot;]])&lt;br /&gt;, | Producer    = [[Don Gant]]&lt;br /&gt;, | Last album  = ''[[Rancho Deluxe (soundtrack)|Rancho Deluxe]]''&amp;lt;br /&amp;gt;(1975)&lt;br /&gt;, | This album  = '''''Havaña Daydreamin' '''''&amp;lt;br /&amp;gt;(1976)&lt;br /&gt;, | Next album  = ''[[Changes in Latitudes, Changes in Attitudes]]'&amp;lt;br /&amp;gt;(1977)&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, '''''Havana Daydreamin''''''&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;The lettering on the album cover and the [[compact disc|CD]] shows '''''Havaña Daydreamin'''''' with an &amp;quot;[[ñ]]&amp;quot; in &amp;quot;[[Havana]]&amp;quot;. This was noted in a critique in ''[[Stereo Review]]'' Volume 37 1976, which says &amp;quot;There is certainly pleasure aplenty ... in 'Havaña [sic] Daydreamin',' [Buffet's] latest disc for ABC/Dunhill&amp;quot;, but which refers to the title track as &amp;quot;the title song, Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot;.&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; is the seventh [[album]] by [[United States|American]] popular music [[singer-songwriter]] [[Jimmy Buffett]] and his fourth regular major label album.  It was produced by [[Don Gant]] and released in January 1976 as [[ABC Dunhill Records|ABC Dunhill]] ABCD-914, later rereleased on ABC Dunhill's successor label [[MCA Records|MCA]].&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Alternate versions==&lt;br /&gt;, The album's name was originally to have been ''Kick It in Second Wind'' and was to have included the songs &amp;quot;Please Take Your Drunken 15 Year Old Girlfriend Home,&amp;quot; &amp;quot;Train to Dixieland,&amp;quot; and &amp;quot;Wonder Why We Ever Go Home&amp;quot; as well as a different version of &amp;quot;Kick It in Second Wind.&amp;quot;  Instead, these songs were replaced with &amp;quot;Woman Goin' Crazy on Caroline Street&amp;quot;, &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot;, and &amp;quot;Cliches.&amp;quot;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;[http://www.buffettworld.com/discography/havana_daydreamin'.html Havana Daydreamin'] at Buffett World.&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;  &amp;quot;Wonder Why We Ever Go Home&amp;quot; would appear on next album ''[[Changes in Latitudes, Changes in Attitudes]]''.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Several rare versions of this album exist or are rumored to. These have altered song ordering and contain one or more of the songs &amp;quot;Please Take Your Drunken 15 Year Old Girlfriend Home,&amp;quot; &amp;quot;Train to Dixieland,&amp;quot; and &amp;quot;We've Been Taken to the Cleaners (and I Already Had my Shirts Done).&amp;quot;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;[http://www.buffettremasters.com/discography/havana.htm Havana Daydreamin'] at BuffettRemasters.com&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Songs==&lt;br /&gt;, Most of the songs on the album were written or co-written by Buffett, two with his future wife, Jane Slagsvol. Other songs include &amp;quot;Big Rig&amp;quot; written by Coral Reefer [[Greg &amp;quot;Fingers&amp;quot; Taylor]] and &amp;quot;This Hotel Room&amp;quot; by [[Steve Goodman]] (who also co-wrote &amp;quot;Woman Goin' Crazy on Caroline Street&amp;quot; with Buffett).  The album also contains a remake of [[Jesse Winchester]]'s &amp;quot;Defying Gravity,&amp;quot; the first of several Winchester songs Buffett would record over his career.  (The song would also be remade by [[Emmylou Harris]].)  None of the songs on the album have been played regularly at Buffett's live concerts since the 1970s.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, A different version of &amp;quot;The Captain and the Kid&amp;quot; was originally released in 1970 on ''[[Down to Earth (Jimmy Buffett album)|Down to Earth]]'' and yet another on 2002's ''[[Meet Me in Margaritaville: The Ultimate Collection]]'' making it (with &amp;quot;In the Shelter&amp;quot;) one of only two Buffett songs with three different studio versions.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, For pacing purposes, the second verse of &amp;quot;Woman Going Crazy on Caroline Street&amp;quot; was cut on the single release.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Chart performance==&lt;br /&gt;, ''Havaña Daydreamin''' was Buffett's most successful album to date reaching #65 on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] album chart and #21 on the [[Top Country Albums|''Billboard'' Top Country Albums]] chart.  However, none of the three [[single (music)|single]]s from the album charted.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Critical reception==&lt;br /&gt;, {{Album ratings&lt;br /&gt;, | rev1 = [[Allmusic]]&lt;br /&gt;, | rev1Score = {{Rating|3|5}}&amp;lt;ref name=Allmusic&amp;gt;{{Allmusic|class=album|id=r2920 |label=Havana Daydreamin'|first= William |last= Ruhlmann|accessdate= September 19, 2012}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, | rev2 = [[Robert Christgau]]&lt;br /&gt;, | rev2Score = (B) &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.robertchristgau.com/get_artist.php?name=Jimmy+Buffet |title=CG: Jimmy Buffet |publisher=Robert Christgau |date= |accessdate=2012-02-20}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, William Ruhlmann of [[Allmusic]] wrote that &amp;quot;By the time of... Havana Daydreamin', Jimmy Buffett seemed to have established a pattern for what a collection of his songs would be.&amp;quot; Ruhlman noted that while the album's style was still essentially the [[country music]] of Buffett's earlier work, this release exemplified his shift in audience from the country scene to the popular market, as well as his adoption of a &amp;quot;Gulf Coast ne'er-do-well&amp;quot; persona.&amp;lt;ref name=Allmusic/&amp;gt; Peter Reilly of ''[[Stereo Review]]'' found the album appealing, saying &amp;quot;I confess that I find it hard to resist anyone who spends so little time trying to impress me&amp;quot;. Reilly found the title track perhaps the best, calling it &amp;quot;an ambiguous trip into [[B. Traven]] (you remember him  ''[[The Treasure of Sierra Madre]]'', ''[[The Death Ship|Death Ship]]'') territory.&amp;quot;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;Reilly, Peter (1976). ''Stereo Review'', volume 37.&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite book |title= Jimmy Buffett Scrapbook |last= Humphrey |first= Mark |last2= Lewine |last1= Harris |year= 2000 |publisher= Citadel Press |isbn= 080652099X |page= 131 | accessdate=October 1, 2012 |url=http://books.google.com/books?id=YVd0A6hluCUC&amp;amp;pg=PA131&amp;amp;lpg=PA131&amp;amp;dq=%22Havana+Daydreamin%27%22+%22b+traven%22&amp;amp;source=bl&amp;amp;ots=ZGsP1hPGKv&amp;amp;sig=e0cGeINIlnTTWXYCzapxnUVLjgY&amp;amp;hl=en&amp;amp;sa=X&amp;amp;ei=b6FpUNGEO5Co8QTqz4CAAQ&amp;amp;ved=0CCwQ6AEwAg#v=onepage&amp;amp;q=%22Havana%20Daydreamin%27%22&amp;amp;f=false }}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; In 2012, Jeff Vrabel of ''[[The Florida Times-Union]]'' listed the track as one of Buffett's &amp;quot;lost treasures&amp;quot;, describing it as &amp;quot;a humid, drifting tale of boats, wine and late-night stories, all wrapped in circumstances that seem darker and more criminal.&amp;quot;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite news |title= Discover Jimmy Buffett's lost musical treasures|author= Jeff Vrabel |url= Jacksonville.com: http://jacksonville.com/entertainment/music/2012-01-27/story/discover-jimmy-buffetts-lost-musical-treasures#ixzz26w0K3uGo |newspaper= [[The Florida Times-Union]] |date= January 27, 2012 |accessdate=September 19, 2012}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Track listing==&lt;br /&gt;, '''Side A:'''&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;Woman Goin' Crazy on Caroline Street&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;(Jimmy Buffett, [[Steve Goodman]])&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  4:08&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;My Head Hurts My Feet Stink and I Don't Love Jesus&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;(Jimmy Buffett)&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  2:35&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;The Captain and the Kid&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;(Jimmy Buffett)&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  3:16&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;Big Rig&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;([[Greg &amp;quot;Fingers&amp;quot; Taylor]])&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  3:30&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;Defying Gravity&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;([[Jesse Winchester]])&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  2:41&lt;br /&gt;, '''Side B:'''&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;Havaña Daydreamin'&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;(Jimmy Buffett)&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  3:38&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;Cliches&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;(Jimmy Buffett)&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  2:45&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;Something So Feminine About a Mandolin&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;(Jimmy Buffett, Jane Slagsvol)&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  3:32&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;Kick It in Second Wind&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;(Jimmy Buffett, Jane Slagsvol)&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  3:56&lt;br /&gt;, #&amp;quot;This Hotel Room&amp;quot; &amp;lt;small&amp;gt;([[Steve Goodman]])&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;  3:07&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Personnel==&lt;br /&gt;, '''The [[Coral Reefer Band]]:'''&lt;br /&gt;, *Jimmy Buffett: Guitar and vocals&lt;br /&gt;, *Roger Bartlett: Guitar&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Greg &amp;quot;Fingers&amp;quot; Taylor]]: Harmonica, piano&lt;br /&gt;, *Harry Dailey: Bass&lt;br /&gt;, *Phillip Fajardo: Drums&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, '''Friends and Honorary Coral Reefers:'''&lt;br /&gt;, *Jerry McGee: Guitar&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Joe Osborn]]: Bass&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Michael Utley|Mike Utley]]: Piano&lt;br /&gt;, *Doyle Gresham: Pedal steel&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Sammy Creason]]: Drums&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Johnny Gimble]]: Fiddle&lt;br /&gt;, *Ferrel Morris: Percussion&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Steve Goodman]]: Guitar&lt;br /&gt;, *[[Don Gant]], [[Buzz Cason]], Bergen White, Ginger Holiday, Anita Bell: Background vocals&lt;br /&gt;, *The [[Oak Ridge Boys]]: Background vocals on &amp;quot;My Head Hurts&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, *Horns on &amp;quot;Big Rig&amp;quot;: [[Muscle Shoals Sound Studio|The Muscle Shoals Horns]]&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Singles==&lt;br /&gt;, *&amp;quot;Havaña Daydreamin'&amp;quot; b/w &amp;quot;Woman Goin' Crazy on Caroline Street&amp;quot; (Released on ABC Dunhill 12220 in July 1976)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==References==&lt;br /&gt;, {{Reflist}}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {{Jimmy Buffett}}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {{DEFAULTSORT:Havana Daydreamin'}}&lt;br /&gt;, [[Category:1976 albums]]&lt;br /&gt;, [[Category:Jimmy Buffett albums]]&lt;br /&gt;, [[Category:ABC Records albums]]&lt;br /&gt;, [[Category:Albums produced by Don Gant]]&lt;/div&gt;,     </summary>,     <author>,       <name>,         Aervanath,       </name>,     </author>,   </entry>,   <entry>,     <id>,       //en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Talk:Havana_Daydreamin%27&amp;diff=516021205,     </id>,     <title>,       Talk:Havana Daydreamin',     </title>,     <link rel="alternate" type="text/html" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Talk:Havana_Daydreamin%27&amp;diff=516021205"/>,     <updated>,       2012-10-04T19:52:21Z,     </updated>,     <summary type="html">,       &lt;p&gt;Aervanath: /* Requested move */ fix; you'd think after being an admin for 4 years I wouldn't make silly mistakes like this anymore... :)&lt;/p&gt;, &lt;hr /&gt;, &lt;div&gt;{{album|class=start}}&lt;br /&gt;, ==28 September 2008==&lt;br /&gt;, I can confirm that some versions of the album include tracks not listed on the album cover or record labels. The album I've owned for many years, (purchased in 1976) includes &amp;quot;Please Take Your Drunken Fifteen Year Old Girlfriend Home&amp;quot;, and omits the tracks &amp;quot;Cliches&amp;quot;, and &amp;quot;Defying Gravity&amp;quot;. There are two slightly different versions of &amp;quot;Kick It In Second Wind&amp;quot;.&lt;br /&gt;, &amp;quot;15 Year Old Girlfriend&amp;quot; is one of my favorite Buffett songs. The lyrics are amusing, and it has a catchy groove to it.&lt;br /&gt;, When I lived in San Diego in the late eighties and early nineties, a DJ on KLOS in L.A. used to kick off the weekend with a trio of songs and &amp;quot;15 Year old Girlfriend&amp;quot; was one of them.&lt;br /&gt;, [[User:KC49er|KC49er]] ([[User talk:KC49er|talk]]) 01:33, 28 September 2008 (UTC)KC49ers&lt;br /&gt;, ==Fair use rationale for Image:JimmyBuffettHavanaDaydreamin'.jpg==&lt;br /&gt;, [[Image:Nuvola apps important.svg|70px|left]]&lt;br /&gt;, '''[[:Image:JimmyBuffettHavanaDaydreamin'.jpg]]''' is being used on this article. Editors desiring to contest the closing decision should consider a [[Wikipedia:move review|move review]]. No further edits should be made to this section. ''&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The result of the move request was: '''moved.''' Wikipedia always follows [[WP:RS|reliable sources]], and &amp;quot;Wikipedia articles should be based mainly on reliable ''secondary'' sources.&amp;quot; If the secondary sources we have refer to the title without the tilde, then we use the title without the tilde, whatever the &amp;quot;original&amp;quot; name of the album/track was intended to be. [[User:Aervanath|Aervanath]] ([[User talk:Aervanath|talk]]) 19:50, 4 October 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ----&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, [[Havaña Daydreamin&amp;amp;#39;]] ? {{no redirect|Havana Daydreamin'}}  The proper name of the album (and its title track of the same name) is &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot;, no tilde.  Never was one.  (See here for reputable source documenting this: http://www.artistdirect.com/nad/store/artist/album/0,,58877,00.html.)  A page by the proper name pre-existed, someone erroneously corrected it to the Spanish language form for the word &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot; (with a tilde).  The errant redirect needs to be undone, and all references to &amp;quot;Havaña&amp;quot; in the (restored) page corrected to &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot;.  Please advise me when the move is complete and I will undertake these latter edits.  Thank you.  [[User:Wikiuser100|Wikiuser100]] ([[User talk:Wikiuser100|talk]]) 00:14, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :'''Not sure'''. Our copy of the album cover image is very low-res and does not clearly show the title lettering, but a full-size image of the album cover clearly shows &amp;quot;Havaña&amp;quot; (searching &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot; at http://images.google.com/ gives many examples, for instance http://whenyouputitthatway.wordpress.com/2012/03/11/appreciating-jimmy-buffett/ ). On the other hand, listening to the title song (on YouTube or elsewhere), it is clearly pronounced &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot;, presumably about the city, and not with the &amp;quot;'ny'-as-in-'canyon'&amp;quot; sound of n-tilde. So this is clearly the tilde equivalent of a [[heavy-metal umlaut]].  The question is, how do we handle this?  We could do something similar to the [[Spinal Tap]] article, keeping it at the non-diacritic title but mentioning the diacritical &amp;quot;flourish&amp;quot; in the lede (I will attempt an edit).  But do we have Spinal Tap at the non-diacritic title because that's the best choice, or simply as a practical matter because n-umlaut is more or less nonexistent in real usage and the diacritic title would not display properly for many users.  [[User:P.T. Aufrette|P.T. Aufrette]] ([[User talk:P.T. Aufrette|talk]]) 02:52, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, * '''&amp;lt;s&amp;gt;Also not sure&amp;lt;/s&amp;gt;''' I must say it irks a bit to see Havana mispelled like that, but it clearly is there on the 1976 LP cover and hasn't been photo-shopped out in the CD reissue. Given the lyrics ''&amp;quot;Stashed his trash in Ecuador / Bought a good suit of clothes / Flew on up to Mexico / Standin' by the shore / Waitin' for some mystery&amp;quot;'' and the apparent reputation of general irony of Jimmy Buffet's Caribbean books and records, have to assume that this is a deliberate stylistic &amp;quot;heavy metal umlaut&amp;quot; as P.T. Aufrette says, not just a mistake. The fact that Havana is overlatinised with a mistaken tilde may be connected with the lyrics' irony about a gringo in Latinland? Who knows. But whatever we can't simply correct it because Havana doesn't have a tilde in real life. I would think first priority is to actually mention the oddity in the lede, not simply remove it as a recent edit has done. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 03:22, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, **'''Oppose''' Stero Review (1976) noted the &amp;quot;mistake,&amp;quot; see source now in article. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 03:49, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Oppose'''.  It's a [[metal umlaut|gulf and western tilde]].  The original release ([http://www.discogs.com/viewimages?release=1297706 images]), the 1980 MCA release ([http://www.discogs.com/viewimages?release=3451888 images]), and the CD release of the album (on the cover and the CD itself, but not on the spine label) all use the tilde.  ''Cf''. [[Mötley Crüe (album)|''Mötley Crüe'' (album)]], ''[[March ör Die]]'', ''[[Ænima]]'', and of course [[Rinôçérôse (album)|''Rinôçérôse'' (album)]].   [[User talk:AjaxSmack|&amp;lt;span style=&amp;quot;border:1px solid #000073;background:#4D4DA6;padding:2px;color:#F9FFFF;text-shadow:black 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em&amp;quot;&amp;gt;&amp;lt;font face=&amp;quot;Georgia&amp;quot;&amp;gt;&amp;amp;nbsp;'''AjaxSmack'''&amp;amp;nbsp;&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt;&amp;lt;/span&amp;gt;]] 03:37, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Support''', per [http://www.worldcat.org/title/havana-daydreamin/oclc/178729216&amp;amp;referer=brief_results WorldCat], [http://www.amazon.com/Havana-Daydreamin/dp/B000W11MM2/ref=sr_1_4?ie=UTF8&amp;amp;qid=1345520957&amp;amp;sr=8-4&amp;amp;keywords=Havana+Daydreamin%27 Amazon], [http://www.cduniverse.com/search/xx/music/pid/1104335/a/Havana+Daydreamin'.htm CD Universe], [http://www.allmusic.com/album/havana-daydreamin-mw0000194138 AllMusic], and the ''[http://books.google.com.vn/books?id=D5Wq1LM7-84C&amp;amp;q=Havana+Daydreamin#search_anchor Standard Catalog of American Records]''. Everyone called it ''Havana Daydreamin`'' even when the official name had a diacritic. It looks like the diacritic-free form is the title proper for the CD, i.e. it has been the official name since 1987. [[User:Kauffner|Kauffner]] ([[User talk:Kauffner|talk]]) 04:42, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::The Amazon CD image clearly shows the &amp;quot;ambiguous journey into B. Traven&amp;quot; tilde. Whether Amazon's inputters can/do input Spanish (particularly incorrect pseudo-Spanish) into indexing is not germane here. [Can't see the track-listing of course, to see whether it is still as the LP or has been dehumorised....] [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 07:09, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :::Album covers are like book covers. They are just art. If the diacritic was part of the title proper, WorldCat would give it. [[User:Kauffner|Kauffner]] ([[User talk:Kauffner|talk]]) 07:32, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::::Are you a librarian, Kauffner? This is a pretty good description of how we catalog, by [[Anglo-American Cataloguing Rules|AACR2]]. If it was cataloged as &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin',&amp;quot; that's what was on the album itself, assuming the cataloger didn't make any mistakes. When cataloging records or CDs, the title on the disc is the &amp;quot;title proper&amp;quot; for librarians. I'm not sure how much it informs this debate, however. --[[User:BDD|BDD]] ([[User talk:BDD|talk]]) 18:21, 4 October 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Oppose'''. I dug out my original '70s LP and sure enough the tilde is on the cover and vinyl album's Side A song list.  Had long since faded from memory (due initially to Buffett ignoring its pronunciation, then decades of it not being used even in the US music media (per current example of artistsdirect.com cited at the start of this thread)).  If we were rewriting history and adding one where it never had been I would continue to oppose its use; accepting reality is something else.  Should have rooted out the old LP to begin with. [[User:Wikiuser100|Wikiuser100]] ([[User talk:Wikiuser100|talk]]) 18:29, 24 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Support'''. This is the epitome of what [[MOS:TM]] is referring to when it says &amp;quot;Avoid using special characters that are not pronounced, are '''included purely for decoration''', or simply substitute for English words (e.g., ? used for &amp;quot;love&amp;quot;).&amp;quot; The title is recorded sans tilda in all the sources currently used, as well as, for instance, here: [http://www.amazon.com/Havana-Daydreamin-Jimmy-Buffett/dp/B000002PBZ][http://www.postandcourier.com/article/20080323/PC1602/303239998][http://jacksonville.com/entertainment/music/2012-01-27/story/discover-jimmy-buffetts-lost-musical-treasures]--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 19:04, 13 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::Hmm, I've had so much recent experience of following MOS pages and then finding they've been edit-warred by editors at odds with article-reality that I daren't even look. If it applies to music it may just mean that whoever's edit is on top there has a problem with articles like [[Mötley Crüe]]. But as above Stero Review (1976) noted the &amp;quot;mistake,&amp;quot; and that source is now in article. We don't know it is &amp;quot;included purely for decoration&amp;quot;, but what does &amp;quot;included purely for decoration&amp;quot; mean anyway? Isn't [[Häagen-Dazs]] purely decoration, designed to trick consumers into thinking it's a Swedish product? I'd still prefer to go with the physical album cover and Stereo Review picking up on it than MOS edits which appear to be at odds with [[Mötley Crüe]] en.wp reality. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 06:58, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :::As you know we follow what the secondary sources say above whatever appeared on the album in the 1970s. Unlike the example of Motley Crue, in this case they virtually all eschew the tilda, evidently including the Stereo Review source after the first mention where they note the error. The sources do this because this is an unpronounced, unaddressed decorative element, or else an error, neither of which warrant us including it against use in the sources.--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 13:13, 18 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::::Yeah, well in any case [[User:Wikiuser100|Wikiuser100]] no longer supports his own proposal. Stan Zimmerman uses Ponce de León so he counts (against by omission) the mispelled Havana... but otherwise the sources don't carry Spanish even when correct. I'm not particularly bothered, as I (the [[Spanish orthography]] part of me) would like to correct it. Given he doesn't mention the song in his own books, maybe someone should email him? Anyway this has been an interesting/entertaining little time-waster. Cheers. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 10:20, 19 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :::::Once again, it doesn't matter what Buffett calls it, it matters what the sources call it. The only source we've seen that includes it is Stereo Review, which merely notes the error with a [''sic''] - and then calls it &amp;quot;Hava'''n'''a Daydreamin'&amp;quot; elsewhere in the text. Of the other sources, Allmusic.com is [http://www.allmusic.com/album/carlos-nunez-en-concert-mw0000742788 clearly capable] of using diacritics, but avoids them with this album.[http://www.allmusic.com/album/havana-daydreamin-mw0000194138] Whether the other sources use Spanish orthography in general is immaterial, since this isn't Spanish orthography, it's just a decorative (and erroneous) element on an English-language album. At any rate, they certainly don't use the tilda. We have specific guidelines against using these things; this case is pretty clear cut.--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 15:01, 19 September 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::::::[http://books.google.com/books?id=YVd0A6hluCUC&amp;amp;pg=PA131&amp;amp;lpg=PA131&amp;amp;dq=%22Havana+Daydreamin%27%22+%22b+traven%22&amp;amp;source=bl&amp;amp;ots=ZGsP1hPGKv&amp;amp;sig=e0cGeINIlnTTWXYCzapxnUVLjgY&amp;amp;hl=en&amp;amp;sa=X&amp;amp;ei=b6FpUNGEO5Co8QTqz4CAAQ&amp;amp;ved=0CCwQ6AEwAg#v=onepage&amp;amp;q=%22Havana%20Daydreamin%27%22&amp;amp;f=false This book] also calls it &amp;quot;Hava'''n'''a Daydreamin'&amp;quot;, and suggests our current cite of the ''Stereo Review'' piece is incomplete.--[[User:Cuchullain|Cúchullain]] [[User talk:Cuchullain|&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;t&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;]]/[[Special:Contributions/Cuchullain|&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;c&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;]] 14:01, 1 October 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :''The above discussion is preserved as an archive of a [[WP:RM|requested move]].  &amp;lt;span style=&amp;quot;color:red&amp;quot;&amp;gt;'''Please do not modify it.'''&amp;lt;/span&amp;gt; Subsequent comments should be made in a new section on this talk page or in a [[WP:move review|move review]]. Wikipedia always follows [[WP:RS|reliable sources]], and &amp;quot;Wikipedia articles should be based mainly on reliable ''secondary'' sources.&amp;quot; If the secondary sources we have refer to the title without the tilde, then we use the title without the tilde, whatever the &amp;quot;original&amp;quot; name of the album/track was intended to be. [[User:Aervanath|Aervanath]] ([[User talk:Aervanath|talk]]) 19:50, 4 October 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ----&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, [[Havaña Daydreamin&amp;amp;#39;]] ? {{no redirect|Havana Daydreamin'}}  The proper name of the album (and its title track of the same name) is &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot;, no tilde.  Never was one.  (See here for reputable source documenting this: http://www.artistdirect.com/nad/store/artist/album/0,,58877,00.html.)  A page by the proper name pre-existed, someone erroneously corrected it to the Spanish language form for the word &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot; (with a tilde).  The errant redirect needs to be undone, and all references to &amp;quot;Havaña&amp;quot; in the (restored) page corrected to &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot;.  Please advise me when the move is complete and I will undertake these latter edits.  Thank you.  [[User:Wikiuser100|Wikiuser100]] ([[User talk:Wikiuser100|talk]]) 00:14, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :'''Not sure'''. Our copy of the album cover image is very low-res and does not clearly show the title lettering, but a full-size image of the album cover clearly shows &amp;quot;Havaña&amp;quot; (searching &amp;quot;Havana Daydreamin'&amp;quot; at http://images.google.com/ gives many examples, for instance http://whenyouputitthatway.wordpress.com/2012/03/11/appreciating-jimmy-buffett/ ). On the other hand, listening to the title song (on YouTube or elsewhere), it is clearly pronounced &amp;quot;Havana&amp;quot;, presumably about the city, and not with the &amp;quot;'ny'-as-in-'canyon'&amp;quot; sound of n-tilde. So this is clearly the tilde equivalent of a [[heavy-metal umlaut]].  The question is, how do we handle this?  We could do something similar to the [[Spinal Tap]] article, keeping it at the non-diacritic title but mentioning the diacritical &amp;quot;flourish&amp;quot; in the lede (I will attempt an edit).  But do we have Spinal Tap at the non-diacritic title because that's the best choice, or simply as a practical matter because n-umlaut is more or less nonexistent in real usage and the diacritic title would not display properly for many users.  [[User:P.T. Aufrette|P.T. Aufrette]] ([[User talk:P.T. Aufrette|talk]]) 02:52, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, * '''&amp;lt;s&amp;gt;Also not sure&amp;lt;/s&amp;gt;''' I must say it irks a bit to see Havana mispelled like that, but it clearly is there on the 1976 LP cover and hasn't been photo-shopped out in the CD reissue. Given the lyrics ''&amp;quot;Stashed his trash in Ecuador / Bought a good suit of clothes / Flew on up to Mexico / Standin' by the shore / Waitin' for some mystery&amp;quot;'' and the apparent reputation of general irony of Jimmy Buffet's Caribbean books and records, have to assume that this is a deliberate stylistic &amp;quot;heavy metal umlaut&amp;quot; as P.T. Aufrette says, not just a mistake. The fact that Havana is overlatinised with a mistaken tilde may be connected with the lyrics' irony about a gringo in Latinland? Who knows. But whatever we can't simply correct it because Havana doesn't have a tilde in real life. I would think first priority is to actually mention the oddity in the lede, not simply remove it as a recent edit has done. [[User:In ictu oculi|In ictu oculi]] ([[User talk:In ictu oculi|talk]]) 03:49, 21 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, *'''Oppose'''.  It's a [[metal umlaut|gulf and western tilde]].  The original release ([http://www.discogs.com/viewimages?release=1297706 images]), the 1980 MCA release ([http://www.discogs.com/viewimages?release=3451888 images]), and the CD release of the album (on the cover and the CD itself, but not on the spine label) all use the tilde.  ''Cf''. Everyone called it ''Havana Daydreamin`'' even when the official name had a diacritic. &lt;p&gt;Aervanath: Aervanath moved page Mainland Chinese Braille script to Mainland Chinese Braille: see discussion at Talk:Refreshable_braille_display#Moves.3F&lt;/p&gt;, &lt;hr /&gt;, &lt;div&gt;{{for|Chinese braille of Taiwan|Taiwanese Braille}}&lt;br /&gt;, {{Infobox writing system&lt;br /&gt;, | name = Chinese Braille&lt;br /&gt;, | altname = {{Braille cell|background=tansparent|?|?|?|?|?|?| |?|?|?|?|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, | type = [[Semisyllabary]]&lt;br /&gt;, | typedesc = &lt;br /&gt;, | time = &lt;br /&gt;, | languages = [[Standard Chinese]]&lt;br /&gt;, | fam1 = [[Night writing]]&lt;br /&gt;, | fam2 = [[Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, | creator = &lt;br /&gt;, | sample = &lt;br /&gt;, | imagesize = &lt;br /&gt;, | note = none&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, {{SpecialChars}}&lt;br /&gt;, {{Chinese|collapse=no&lt;br /&gt;, |t=???? |s=???? |p=Xiànxíng Mángwén&lt;br /&gt;, |l=Current Braille&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, '''(Mainland) Chinese Braille''' is a [[braille]] script used for [[Standard Chinese]] in mainland [[China]]. Consonants and basic finals conform to [[international braille]], but additional finals form a [[semi-syllabary]], as in [[zhuyin]] (bopomofo). Each syllable is written with up to three Braille cells, representing the [[syllable onset|initial]], [[syllable rime|final]], and [[tone (linguistics)|tone]], respectively. In practice tone is generally omitted.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Braille charts ==&lt;br /&gt;, Traditional Chinese Braille is as follows:&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;Vivian Aldridge, 2000 [2002] ''[http://www.braille.ch/pschin-e.htm How is Chinese written in braille?]'' &amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, === Initials ===&lt;br /&gt;, Chinese Braille initials generally follow the [[pinyin]] assignments of international braille. However, ''j, q, x'' are replaced with ''g, k, h'', as the difference is predictable from the final. (This reflects the historical change of ''g, k, h'' (and also ''z, c, s'') to ''j, q, x'' before ''i'' and ''ü''.) The digraphs ''ch, sh, zh'' are assigned to ? (its pronunciation in [[Russian Braille]]), ? (a common pronunciation in [[international braille]]), and ?. ''R'' is assigned to ?, reflecting the old [[Wade-Giles]] transcription of ?j?. (? is used for the final ''er'', the pronunciation of the name of that letter in [[English Braille]].)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! style=&amp;quot;font-weight: bold;&amp;quot; | [[Pinyin]] &lt;br /&gt;, | b||c||d||f||g/j||h/x||r||k/q||l||m||n||p||ch||s||t||z||sh||zh&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! Braille&lt;br /&gt;, | class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |? || class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?|| class=&amp;quot;Unicode&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;font-size:xx-large;&amp;quot; |?&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! style=&amp;quot;font-weight: bold;&amp;quot; | Equivalent [[Braille ASCII]] &lt;br /&gt;, | B||C||D||F||G||H||J||K||L||M||N||P||Q||S||T||Z||:||/&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, === Finals ===&lt;br /&gt;, The finals approximate [[international braille|international]] values for several of the basic vowels (? ''e (o)'', ? ''yi'', ? ''wo'', ? ''wu'', ? ''yü'', ? ''you'', ? ''ei''), but then necessarily diverge. However, there are a few parallels with other braille alphabets: ? ''er'' and ? ''wai'' are pronounced like the names of those letters in [[English braille]]; ? ''ye'', ? ''ya'', and ? ''you'' are pronounced like those letters in [[Russian Braille]]. {{bc|type=t|ç}} ''yuan'', {{bc|type=t|23456}} ''yue'', {{bc|type=t|gh}} ''yin'', are similar to the [[French Braille#History|old French pronunciations]] ''oin, ieu, in.'' For the most part, however, Chinese Braille finals do not obviously derive from previous conventions. &lt;br /&gt;, {| &lt;br /&gt;, |- valign=top&lt;br /&gt;, |&lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot; &lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, !Pinyin!!Braille&lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, |yu, -ü||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, |yue, -üe||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, |yuan, -üan||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, |yun, -ün||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, |yong, -iong||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, |er||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, === Tones ===&lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | style=&amp;quot;font-weight: bold;&amp;quot; | Tone ||1||2||3||4||neutral&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | style=&amp;quot;font-weight: bold;&amp;quot; | Pinyin ||¯||´||?||`||(none)&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! Braille&lt;br /&gt;, |{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}|| {{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}|| {{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}|| {{braille cell|type=6dot|size=30px|?}}||(none)&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, === Punctuation ===&lt;br /&gt;, Chinese Braille punctuation approximates the form of international braille punctuation, but most use two cells rather than one. For example, the period is {{braille cell|type=text|?|?}}, which is the same pattern and the international single-cell norm of {{braille cell|type=text|dd}}. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable nowrap&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | style=&amp;quot;font-weight: bold;&amp;quot; | Print ||?||,||?||!||:||;||-||||· ([[interpunct]])||(||)||[ ]&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center &lt;br /&gt;, ! Chinese Braille&lt;br /&gt;, |{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}||{{braille cell|type=6dot|size=20px|?|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center &lt;br /&gt;, ! French equivalent&lt;br /&gt;, |{{braille cell|type=text|dd}}||{{braille cell|type=text|comma}}||{{braille cell|type=text|en}}||{{braille cell|type=text|!}}||{{braille cell|type=text|:}}||{{braille cell|type=text|;}}||{{braille cell|type=text|hyphen}}||{{braille cell|type=text|'|'|'}}||{{braille cell|type=text|}}||{{braille cell|type=text|hh}}||{{braille cell|type=text|jj}}||{{braille cell|type=text|()}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, === Rules ===&lt;br /&gt;, *Spaces are added between words, rather than between syllables.&lt;br /&gt;, *Tone is marked only in case of necessity. It is represented immediately after the final.&lt;br /&gt;, *As in [[zhuyin]], the finals of the syllables ''zi, ci, si, zhi, chi, shi, ri'' are not marked.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, :Example:&lt;br /&gt;, :{|&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | colspan=4|&amp;lt;font lang=&amp;quot;zh-cn&amp;quot;&amp;gt;??????&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt; (&amp;lt;font lang=&amp;quot;zh-tw&amp;quot;&amp;gt;??????&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt;)&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | &amp;lt;font size=6&amp;gt;?????&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt; ||?&amp;lt;font size=6&amp;gt;????&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt; ||?&amp;lt;font size=6&amp;gt;????&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt; ||?&amp;lt;font size=6&amp;gt;????&amp;lt;/font&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | ''Shíji?n ||''bù ||''z?o ||''le!''&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | time ||not ||early ||[[perfective|{{sc|pfv}}]]&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, === Ambiguity ===&lt;br /&gt;, Chinese Braille has the same level of ambiguity that pinyin does. In practice, tone is omitted 95% of the time, which leads to a space saving of a third. Tone is also omitted in pinyin military telegraphy, and causes little confusion in context. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The initial pairs ''g/j'', ''k/q'', ''h/x'' are distinguished by the final: initials ''j, q, x'' are followed by the vowels ''i'' or ''ü'', while the initials ''g, k, h'' are followed by other vowels. This reflects the historical derivation of ''j, q, x'' from ''g, k, h'' before ''i'' and ''ü'',&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;They also derive from ''z, c, s'' before ''i'' or ''ü'', and this is the identity reflected in [[Taiwanese braille]].&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; and parallels the dual pronunciations of ''c'' and ''g'' in [[Spanish alphabet|Spanish]] and [[Italian alphabet|Italian]]. In pinyin, the redundancy is resolved in the other direction, with the diaeresis omitted from ''ü'' after ''j, q, x''. Thus braille ?gü? is equivalent to pinyin ''ju'': ?? ''ju'', ?? ''gu''.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Usage ==&lt;br /&gt;, The China Library for the Blind (???????) in Beijing has several thousand volumes, mostly published by the China Braille Press (???????).&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web|last=Fruchterman |first=Jim |url=http://benetech.blogspot.com/2008/10/china-braille-press.html |title=Beneblog: Technology Meets Society: China Braille Press |publisher=Benetech.blogspot.com |date=2008-10-08 |accessdate=2012-08-13}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The [[National Taiwan Library]] has a Braille room with a postal mail service and some electronic documents.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=http://southernlibrarianship.icaap.org/content/v10n01/chen_c01.html |title=Delivery of Library Materials |publisher=Southernlibrarianship.icaap.org |date= |accessdate=2012-08-13}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == See also ==&lt;br /&gt;, * [[Two-Cell Chinese Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, * [[Taiwanese Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, * [[Cantonese Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Further Reading ==&lt;br /&gt;, *{{cite book|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=KFNGAAAAYAAJ&amp;amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;amp;source=gbs_ge_summary_r&amp;amp;cad=0#v=onepage&amp;amp;q&amp;amp;f=false|edition=|year=|location=Printed by Gilbert &amp;amp; Rivington, Limited, St. John's House, Clerkenwell, London E.C.|isbn=|title=Work for the blind in China|author=Constance Frederica Gordon Cumming|publisher=Gilbert &amp;amp; Rivington, Ld.|page=|page=79|quote=|accessdate=2012 23 April}}[Original from Columbia University Digitized Aug 18, 2009]&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == References ==&lt;br /&gt;, *J Grotz, &amp;quot;The necessary reform of Chinese Braille writing&amp;quot;, Rehabilitation (Stuttgart) 1991 Aug 30(3):153-5.
