Thank you. &amp;lt;!-- Talk:Refreshable Braille display crosspost --&amp;gt; [[User:RMCD bot|RMCD bot]] 16:25, 13 August 2012 (UTC)&lt;/div&gt;,     </summary>,     <author>,       <name>,         Aervanath,       </name>,     </author>,   </entry>,   <entry>,     <id>,       //en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Korean_braille&amp;diff=516017730,     </id>,     <title>,       Korean braille,     </title>,     <link rel="alternate" type="text/html" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Korean_braille&amp;diff=516017730"/>,     <updated>,       2012-10-04T19:31:18Z,     </updated>,     <summary type="html">,       &lt;p&gt;Aervanath: Aervanath moved page Korean braille to Korean Braille: see discussion at Talk:Refreshable_Braille_display#Moves.3F&lt;/p&gt;, &lt;hr /&gt;, &lt;div&gt;#REDIRECT [[Korean Braille]]&lt;/div&gt;,     </summary>,     <author>,       <name>,         Aervanath,       </name>,     </author>,   </entry>,   <entry>,     <id>,       //en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Korean_Braille&amp;diff=516017675,     </id>,     <title>,       Korean Braille,     </title>,     <link rel="alternate" type="text/html" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Korean_Braille&amp;diff=516017675"/>,     <updated>,       2012-10-04T19:31:02Z,     </updated>,     <summary type="html">,       &lt;p&gt;Aervanath: Aervanath moved page Korean braille to Korean Braille: see discussion at Talk:Refreshable_Braille_display#Moves.3F&lt;/p&gt;, &lt;hr /&gt;, &lt;div&gt;{{Infobox writing system&lt;br /&gt;, | name = Korean Braille&lt;br /&gt;, | altname = ????????&amp;lt;!--? on its own is 'ja'--&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, | mode = Tactile&lt;br /&gt;, | type = [[alphabet]]&lt;br /&gt;, | typedesc =, [[syllabary|syllabically]] marked&lt;br /&gt;, | time = &lt;br /&gt;, | languages = Korean&lt;br /&gt;, | fam1 = [[Night writing]]&lt;br /&gt;, | fam2 = [[Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, | creator = &lt;br /&gt;, | sample = &lt;br /&gt;, | imagesize = &lt;br /&gt;, | note = none&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, {{Infobox Korean name&lt;br /&gt;, | hangul  = ?? ??&lt;br /&gt;, | hanja   = ?? ??&lt;br /&gt;, | rr      = hangeul jeomja&lt;br /&gt;, | mr      = hang?l ch?mja&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, {{BrailleChars}}&lt;br /&gt;, {{Korean romanization}}&lt;br /&gt;, '''Korean Braille''' is the [[braille alphabet]] of the [[Korean language]]. It is not graphically related to other braille scripts found around the world. Instead, it reflects the patterns found in [[hangul]], and differentiates initial consonants, vowels, and final consonants.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Charts==&lt;br /&gt;, There are also characters for grammatical devices and for punctuation. Numerals are similar to those of other braille systems.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===Consonants===&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Consonants have different syllable-initial and -final variants, capturing some of the feel of hangul. The initial and final variants have the same shapes, but are shifted across the braille block. There are two patterns: The consonants that span the width of the block are shifted one space downward when final. Those that don't span the width of the block are on the right side of the block when initial, but on the left side when final. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, No consonant occupies more than two rows. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, There is no initial version of ''ng''. Initial ''ieung'' in hangul is not written in Korean Braille. However, the expected form is reserved and may not serve other uses, such as punctuation. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {|  class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |-  align=center&lt;br /&gt;, |  style=&amp;quot;font-weight: bold;&amp;quot; | Roman || g || n || d || r || m || b || s || j || ch || k || t || p || h || ng&lt;br /&gt;, |-  align=center&lt;br /&gt;, |  style=&amp;quot;font-weight: bold;&amp;quot; | hangul || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ?&lt;br /&gt;, |- &lt;br /&gt;, ! rowspan=2| initial &lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|4}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|14}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|42}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|5}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|15}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|45}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|6}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|46}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|56}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|142}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|125}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|145}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|425}} &lt;br /&gt;, ! rowspan=2| &amp;amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} &lt;br /&gt;, |- &lt;br /&gt;, ! rowspan=2| final &lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|1}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|25}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|53}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|2}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|26}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|12}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|3}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|13}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|23}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|253}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|236}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|256}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|536}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|2536}}&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}} || {{bc|type=t|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===Vowels===&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, All vowels span the width and height of the block. Because the consonants are specifically syllable initial or syllable final, a syllable that begins with a vowel causes no confusion when written without ''ieung''. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The simpler vowels reflect the symmetries of hangul: the ''yinyang'' pairs ''a, eo'' and ''o, u'' are related through inversion, and yotization of ''a, eo, o, u'' is indicated by reflecting the vowel. This creates a different pattern of symmetry than in hangul. The graphically similar hangul letters ''i'' and ''eu'' are also related by reflection. The ''w'' in ''wa, wo'' is indicated by making the left side of the block solid, while the ''i'' in ''ui, oe'' is shown by making the right side solid. However, the diphthongs ''e, ae'' and their yotized variants show no such patterns. &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Four [[diphthongs]] are represented with two braille blocks, by adding ? to the appropriate vowel for the final element ''-i''.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! Roman &lt;br /&gt;, | a || ya || eo || yeo || o || yo || u || yu || eu || i || e || ae || ye || ui || wa || wo || oe || yae || wae || we || wi&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! hangul &lt;br /&gt;, | ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ? || ?&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! rowspan=2|braille&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|126}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|453}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|423}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|156}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|136}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|436}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|143}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|146}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|426}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|153}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|1453}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|1253}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|43}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|4256}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|1236}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|1423}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|14536}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|453|1253}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|1236|1253}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|1423|1253}} || {{Braille Cell|type=Korean|143|1253}}&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, | {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?|?}} || {{bc|type=text|?|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ===Abbreviations===&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Korean Braille also has several single cell syllable defined. Several are simply the braille cell for an initial consonant, with an assumed vowel &amp;quot;a&amp;quot; added. Some make use of unused cell definitions, while others utilize multi-cell abbreviations, often using malformed consonant clusters or consonant/vowel combinations otherwise abbreviated.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ! It used a cell 4 dots wide by 2 dots high, like [[New York Point]]. 6-dot braille was adapted to Korean by [[Park Du-seong]] in 1926. There have since been a number of revisions. The current form was announced in 1994.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Sources==&lt;br /&gt;, * [http://infor.kbll.or.kr/ Korean Braille library] (in Korean); chart is here[http://infor.kbll.or.kr/images/info/braille_img05.gif]&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {{Braille}}&lt;br /&gt;, {{list of writing systems}}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, [[Category:Korean language|Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, [[Category:Innovative braille scripts]]&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, [[es:Braille coreano]]&lt;br /&gt;, [[fr:Braille coréen]]&lt;br /&gt;, [[ko:?? Aervanath moved page Japanese braille to Japanese Braille: see discussion at Talk:Refreshable_braille_display#Moves.3F&lt;/p&gt;, &lt;hr /&gt;, &lt;div&gt;{{Infobox writing system&lt;br /&gt;, | name = Japanese Braille&lt;br /&gt;, | altname = {{Braille cell|lang=japanese braille|type=text|background=transparent|?|?|?|?|?|?|?}}&lt;br /&gt;, | type = [[Abugida]]&lt;br /&gt;, | typedesc = &lt;br /&gt;, | time = &lt;br /&gt;, | languages = Japanese&lt;br /&gt;, | fam1 = [[Night writing]]&lt;br /&gt;, | fam2 = [[Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, | creator = &lt;br /&gt;, | children = [[Two-Cell Chinese Braille]] (in conception)&lt;br /&gt;, | sample = &lt;br /&gt;, | imagesize = &lt;br /&gt;, | note = none&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, [[Image:Asahi-super-dry-beer-top-of-can-with-braille.jpg|thumb|right|Japanese Braille on a can of Asahi Super Dry beer, written &amp;quot;[[sake]]&amp;quot;]]&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, '''Japanese Braille''' is the [[braille]] script of the [[Japanese language]]. It is based on the original braille script, though the connection is tenuous. In Japanese it is known as {{nihongo|''tenji''|??|}}, literally &amp;quot;dot characters&amp;quot;. Below is a basic chart of Japanese Braille with the Japanese [[hiragana]] character followed by the standard [[roman character]] reading above each braille character.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Japanese Braille is a vowel-based [[abugida]]. That is, the glyphs are syllabic, but unlike [[kana]] contain separate symbols for consonant and vowel, and the vowel takes primacy. The vowels are written in the upper left corner (points 1, 2, 4) and may be used alone. The consonants are written in the lower right corner (points 3, 5, 6) and cannot occur alone.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;An isolated ''t'' would be read as ''wo'', for example. The only exception is ''m'', which when written alone is the syllabic nasal, which may be a design feature rather than coincidence, as the syllabic nasal derives from historic ''mu.''&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; However, the [[semivowel]] ''y'' is indicated by point 4, one of the vowel points, and the vowel combination is dropped to the bottom of the block. When this point is written in isolation, it indicates that the following syllable has a [[youon|medial ''y,'']] as in ''mya.'' For syllables beginning with ''w'' the vowel is also dropped, but no consonant is written.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;Except for the syllable ''wa,'' historic ''w'' is silent in modern Japanese.&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Main chart==&lt;br /&gt;, To the vowels are assigned the international braille patterns of the upper-left half of the cell (dots 1-2-4) in numerical order: ????? (or, equivalently, the first 5 letters of Braille's alphabet, ?????, rotated to fit the available space). The consonantal diacritics, on the other hand, have no apparent connection to international values or numerical order, corresponding as they do to punctuation and formatting marks.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, For illustration, the vowel points are written in black, and the consonant points in green. There is no such distinction in braille as it is actually used.&amp;lt;ref name=tenji&amp;gt;{{cite web|title=????????? (tenji o yonde miyoo)|url=http://www.braille.jp/topics/yonndemiyo.html|publisher=Braille Authority of Japan|accessdate=2012-05-10}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;text-align:center&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;background:#f2f2f2&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | rowspan=&amp;quot;2&amp;quot; | &amp;amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;, | ? wa&lt;br /&gt;, | ? (w)i&lt;br /&gt;, |  &lt;br /&gt;, | ? (w)e&lt;br /&gt;, | ? (w)o&lt;br /&gt;, | &amp;amp;nbsp;&amp;amp;nbsp;-w-&lt;br /&gt;, |-&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|WA}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|WI}}&lt;br /&gt;, | &lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|WE}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|WO}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|26}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Other symbols==&lt;br /&gt;, In kana, a small ''tsu'' (?), called ''[[sokuon]]'', is used to indicate that the following consonant is [[geminate]], and in [[interjection]]s as a [[glottal stop]]. In katakana only, a long vowel is indicated with dash, ?, called a [[ch?on]]. This also looks like a dash in braille:&amp;lt;ref name=tenji /&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;text-align:center&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;background:#f2f2f2&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | ''sokuon''&lt;br /&gt;, | ''ch?on''&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;font-family: monospace&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|2}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|25}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The placement of these blocks mirrors the equivalent kana: the ''sokuon'' indicates that the following consonant is geminant, whereas the ''ch?on'' indicates that the preceding vowel is long.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, In kana, the [[voiced consonant]]s ''g, z, d, b'' are derived from the voiceless consonants ''k, s, t, h'' by adding a [[diacritic]] called ''[[dakuten]]'' to the kana, as in ? ''gi''; in foreign words, ''vu'' is written by adding this to the vowel ''u''. Similarly, ''p'' is derived from ''h'' by adding a small circle, ''[[handakuten]]''. Two kana are fused into a single syllable by writing the second small, as in ?? ''kya'' from ''ki + ya''; this is called ''[[y?on]]''. &amp;lt;ref name=tenji /&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, In Japanese Braille, the signs for these are prefixes. That is, the order is ''dakuten + ki'' for ? ''gi''. When more than one occurs in a single syllable, they are combined in a single prefix block, as the ''y?on-dakuten'' used for ?? ''gya''. &amp;lt;ref name=tenji /&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;text-align:center&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;background:#f2f2f2&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | ''dakuten''&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;(voice)&lt;br /&gt;, | ''handakuten''&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;(p-)&lt;br /&gt;, | ''y?on''&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;(-y-)&lt;br /&gt;, | ''y?on +&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;dakuten''&lt;br /&gt;, | ''y?on +&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;handakuten''&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;font-family: monospace&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|5}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|6}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|4}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|45}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|46}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, The ''y?on'' prefix uses the point that represents ''y'' in the blocks ''ya, yu, yo.'' When placed before ''ka, ku, ko,'' it produces ''kya, kyu, kyo.'' Likewise, the ''y?on-dakuten'' prefix before ''ka, ku, ko'' creates ''gya, gyu, gyo.'' And so on for the other consonants.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Unlike kana, which uses a subscript ''e'', in braille the ''-ye'' in foreign borrowings is written with ''y?on'' and the kana from the ''e'' row: that is, ''kye, she, che, nye, hye, mye, rye'', voiced ''gye, je, bye,'' and plosive ''pye'' are written with the ''y?on'' prefixes plus ''ke, se, te, ne, he, me, re.'' The syllable ''ye'' is written ''y?on'' plus ''e.''&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, There is also a prefix for medial ''-w-'' called ''g?y?on''. When combined with ''ka,'' it produces the obsolete syllable ''kwa.'' It may also be fused with the voicing prefix for ''gwa.'' For foreign borrowings, this extends to ''kwi, kwe, kwo'' and ''gwa gwi gwe gwo''. ''G?y?on'' may also be combined with the vowels ''i, e, o'' for foreign ''wi, we, wo'' (now that the ''w'' in the original Japanese kana for ''wi, we, wo'' is silent); with ''ha, hi, he, ho'' for ''fa, fi, fe, fo'' and (when voiced) for ''va, vi, ve, vo''; and with ''ta, chi, te, to'' for ''tsa, tsi, tse, tso''. These two prefixes are identical to the question mark and full stop.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;text-align:center&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;background:#f2f2f2&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | ''g?y?on''&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;(-w-)&lt;br /&gt;, | ''g?y?on +&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;dakuten''&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;font-family: monospace&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|26}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|256}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, These all parallel usage in kana. However, there are additional conventions which are unique to braille. ''Y?on'' and ''y?on-dakuten'' are also added to ''chi'' and ''shi'' to write ''ti, di'' and ''si, zi'' found in foreign borrowings; similarly ''g?y?on'' and ''g?y?on-dakuten'' are added to ''tsu'' to write ''tu, du''. This differs from the system used in kana, where the base syllables are ''te'' and ''to'' respectively, and a subscript vowel ''i'' or ''u'' is added.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, In an assignment that is counter-intuitive in kana, ''y?on + handakuten'' is prefixed to ''tsu, yu, yo'' to produce ''tyu, fyu, fyo'' in foreign words, and voiced for ''dyu, vyu, vyo''. The latter''y?on + dakuten + handakuten'', is impossible in kana:&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;text-align:center&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;background:#f2f2f2&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | ''y?on +&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;dakuten +&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;handakuten''&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;font-family: monospace&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille Cell|type=kana|456}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Punctuation==&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Besides the punctuation of Japanese, braille also has symbols to indicate that the following characters are [[Hindu numeral]]s or the [[Latin alphabet]].&amp;lt;ref name=tenji /&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot; style=&amp;quot;text-align:center&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;background:#f2f2f2&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | ?&lt;br /&gt;, | ?&lt;br /&gt;, | ?&lt;br /&gt;, | ?&lt;br /&gt;, | ? ?&lt;br /&gt;, | ( )&lt;br /&gt;, | num.&lt;br /&gt;, | Latin&lt;br /&gt;, | upper case&lt;br /&gt;, | hyph.&lt;br /&gt;, |- style=&amp;quot;font-family: monospace&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|256|}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|56|}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|26}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|253}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|36}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|2536}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|4536|}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|56|}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|6}}&lt;br /&gt;, | {{Braille cell|type=image|36|}}&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, There are several additional punctuation marks, including one to indicate that the following characters are English words and not just in the Latin alphabet.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==External links==&lt;br /&gt;, *[http://www.braille.jp/en/ The Braille Authority of Japan] -- the Aervanath moved page Cantonese braille to Cantonese Braille: see discussion at Talk:Refreshable_braille_display#Moves.3F&lt;/p&gt;, &lt;hr /&gt;, &lt;div&gt;{{Infobox writing system&lt;br /&gt;, | name = Cantonese Braille&lt;br /&gt;, | altname = {{bc|background=transparent|t|ff|1|c|i|2}}&lt;br /&gt;, | type = [[semisyllabary]]&lt;br /&gt;, | typedesc = &lt;br /&gt;, | time = &lt;br /&gt;, | languages = [[Cantonese language|Cantonese]]&lt;br /&gt;, | fam1 = [[Braille]]&lt;br /&gt;, | fam2 = &lt;br /&gt;, | creator = &lt;br /&gt;, | sample = &lt;br /&gt;, | imagesize = &lt;br /&gt;, | note = none&lt;br /&gt;, }}&lt;br /&gt;, '''Cantonese Braille''' ([[Chinese language|Chinese:]] ????) is a [[braille]] script used to write [[Cantonese language|Cantonese]] in [[Hong Kong]]. It is locally referred as ''tim chi'' (?? ''dim2zi6'') 'dot characters', or more commonly but ambiguously ''tuk chi'' (??) 'raised characters'.  Although Cantonese is written in [[Chinese character]]s, Cantonese Braille is purely phonetic, with punctuation, digits, and [[Latin letters]] from the original Braille.  It can be mixed with [[English language|English]] text.&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Charts==&lt;br /&gt;, Each syllable is divided into three parts: the initial consonant, the rime (vowel and any final consonant), and the tone. For example, ? ''pun4'' is written ?{{bc|?|?|?}}?, with initial ''p'', final ''un'', and tone ''4''.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;Jennie Lam Suk Yin, 2003, [http://hub.hku.hk/bitstream/10722/40646/1/FullText.pdf Confusion of tones in visually-impaired children using Cantonese braille] (Archived by WebCite® at http://www.webcitation.org/6AK0HT0Vk)&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; (See [[Cantonese phonology]].) Among initials, aspirated consonants (''p t ts k kw = p' t' ts' k' kw'&amp;lt;/i&amp;gt;) are derived by adding dots to the unaspirated consonants (&amp;lt;i&amp;gt;b d dz g gw = p t ts k kw''):&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |+Initials&lt;br /&gt;, !Braille&lt;br /&gt;, |{{bc|type=i|f}}||{{bc|type=i|h}}||{{bc|type=i|k}}||{{bc|type=i|r}}||{{bc|type=i|l}}||{{bc|type=i|m}}||{{bc|type=i|n}}||{{bc|type=i|p}}||{{bc|type=i|and}}||{{bc|type=i|s}}||{{bc|type=i|t}}||{{bc|type=i|with}}||{{bc|type=i|w}}||{{bc|type=i|j}}||{{bc|type=i|c}}||{{bc|type=i|x}}||{{bc|type=i|q}}||{{bc|type=i|er}}||{{bc|type=i|g}}&lt;br ''ng'' may also be used as rimes (syllabic nasals), in which case they are followed directly by the tone.&lt;br /&gt;, *When ''i'' or ''u'' (but not ''y'') begins a syllable, a dummy consonant ''j'' Otherwise tone is written after the rime, as follows:&lt;br /&gt;, {| class=&amp;quot;wikitable&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;, |+Tones&lt;br /&gt;, !Braille&lt;br /&gt;, |{{bc|type=i|1}}||{{bc|type=i|4}}||{{bc|type=i|3}}||{{bc|type=i|6}}||{{bc|type=i|2}}||{{bc|type=i|5}}||{{bc|type=i|3}}&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, ![[Cantonese Pinyin|Pinyin]]&lt;br /&gt;, |2||3||4||5||6||8||9&lt;br /&gt;, |}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, In numerical order, the cells are as follows: &lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, {| class=wikitable&lt;br /&gt;, ! 0&lt;br /&gt;, !rowspan=6|&amp;amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;, !colspan=10|main sequence ||rowspan=6|&amp;amp;nbsp; ||colspan=2|suppl.&lt;br /&gt;, |- align=center&lt;br /&gt;, |&amp;amp;nbsp;&amp;lt;br&amp;gt;{{Braille &lt;div&gt;{{WP Writing systems|class=start|importance=mid}}&lt;br /&gt;, {{WikiProject Disability|class=start|importance=mid}}&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, == Other languages in Cyrillic? ==&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, Is this braille set used only for Russian language, or also in other Cyrillic script languages? -[[User:DePiep|DePiep]] ([[User talk:DePiep|talk]]) 10:55, 20 April 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, :No. I have documentation from Yugoslavia - it was still in existence when this Unesco report came out - on Serbo-Croation and Macedonian, and while many letters have the same Braille representation, several do not (like ? - ? vs. ?), and a given braille cell (like ?) can represent different letters, like ? vs. ?, where ? is ?. So no, I know it only to be valid for Russian, although I wouldn't be surprised if it were good for other Soviet Union languages. [[User:Vanisaac|Van]][[User talk:Vanisaac|Isaac]]&amp;lt;sub&amp;gt;&amp;lt;small&amp;gt;[[WP:WikiProject Writing systems|WS]]&amp;lt;/small&amp;gt;&amp;lt;/sub&amp;gt;&amp;lt;sup style=&amp;quot;margin-left:-2.9ex&amp;quot;&amp;gt;[[Special:Contributions/Vanisaac|contribs]]&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt; 03:13, 24 April 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, ::That is good facts. Still ... I am expecting that this basic Cyrillic set is used more widely, outside of Russian language. I cannot accept that 24 Slavic &amp;amp; USSR-neighbouring ''languages'' do not use '''these''' Cyrillic ''script'' codes. -[[User:DePiep|DePiep]] ([[User talk:DePiep|talk]]) 20:55, 26 April 2012 (UTC)&lt;br /&gt;, &lt;br /&gt;, ==Move discussion in progress==&lt;br /&gt;, There is a move discussion in progress on [[Talk:Refreshable Braille display#Moves? |Talk:Refreshable Braille display]] which affects this page.
